  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ebe8c850-8977-430b-bd9f-10ce619b61df'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9649302795663561029">Building on her series featuring forensic sculptor Eve Duncan, bestselling suspense writer Iris Johansen takes a slightly different tangent with her latest thriller, <i>The Search</i>. The search and rescue team of Sarah Patrick and her golden retriever, Monty, first appeared in <i>The Killing Game</i>, where they helped Eve track down a kidnapped child and a maniacal killer. Now, John </span>
  <span id="freeText9649302795663561029" style="display:none">Building on her series featuring forensic sculptor Eve Duncan, bestselling suspense writer Iris Johansen takes a slightly different tangent with her latest thriller, <i>The Search</i>. The search and rescue team of Sarah Patrick and her golden retriever, Monty, first appeared in <i>The Killing Game</i>, where they helped Eve track down a kidnapped child and a maniacal killer. Now, John Logan, the billionaire who wooed Eve only to lose her to Joe Quinn, needs to utilize Sarah and Monty's talents in a quest of his own. <br /><br />Although it has it rewards, the rescue work Sarah and Monty do demands a hefty emotional toll from them both. Sarah is highly protective of Monty, and when Logan first approaches her with what's obviously a very dangerous mission, Sarah is quick to say no. But Logan brings his powerful resources to bear and more or less forces Sarah to agree to the mission or face the loss of her job, her peace of mind, and Monty. The task at hand involves finding and rescuing a highly valued scientist who has been kidnapped and is being held somewhere in Colombia. But the man who took the scientist is a ruthless and heartless killer whose primary objective is carrying out his sadistic revenge on Logan. <br /><br />Sarah, none too happy about being coerced into helping Logan, becomes even less inclined toward him when Monty is wounded in the rescue attempt. Logan is wounded too, and after their mission has been accomplished, the threesome end up back at Sarah's isolated cabin. Sarah does everything she can to make Logan leave but finds it hard to be too insistent given his wounds. Besides, when Logan pays his debt to her for completing the mission, it is something Sarah could never have anticipated, an act that leaves her stunned, confused, and indebted. As for Logan, he refuses to leave Sarah alone because he knows that his nemesis, Rudzak, saw her and Monty in Colombia. And because of the nature of his relationship with Rudzak and the secret history they share, Logan knows the psycho will eventually come after Sarah. <br /><br />Holed up together and fighting a wide array of emotions, Sarah and Logan discover a spark of passion between them. Though they both try to resist, eventually the spark ignites a full-fledged conflagration that leaves both of them stunned, puzzled, and forever changed. By the time the inevitable confrontation with Rudzak occurs, Logan will be forced to risk both his life and his heart in hopes of keeping Sarah and Monty safe. And Sarah must risk everything she holds dear if she ever hopes to find a happiness she is only now beginning to realize. <br /><br />Fans of Johansen's previous books in this series, <i>The Face of Deception</i> and <i>The Killing Game</i>, will enjoy brief though hair-raising appearances by Eve, Joe Quinn, and Jane -- the spunky, street-wise child Eve adopted in the last book. Also filling out the character roster is an intriguing love interest for Monty: an injured gray wolf named Maggie. But the best parts of Johansen's latest effort are her characteristically explosive mix of chilling terror and heated passion and her gift for weaving a tale of intrigue where seeing isn't necessarily believing. <br /><br />Beth Amos</span>
  <a data-text-id="9649302795663561029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The books can stand alone, but if you want to follow the personal interactions of the characters, you really should read them in order. Sometimes the <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The books can stand alone, but if you want to follow the personal interactions of the characters, you really should read them in order. Sometimes the books are uneven but I continue to read to follow the characters.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9687023093605345213">3.7 <br/>Best part-Loved the dog rescue and how attentive the owner handler was.<br/>Worst part-The dog handlers choices didn't always follow her talk. <br/>Over all I enjoyed this suspense read. I am a sucker for a book with a dog, got me right there. Then they toped it with a really nasty villain, and sexy alpha man and an equally alpha woman. I was left guessing till the end, which is always nice.<br/>I will go back and read the first 2 books in this series before moving on more.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede"><img alt="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487436758p2/1379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1657343850?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553582123" href="/book/show/1294633.The_Search">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1657343850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer639519575266395076">Iris Johansen has managed to write a story that instead of focusing on Eve Duncan (who is the main character in this series) is putting Sarah Patrick and John Logan in focus and I loved it! I adored John Logan in the first book in the Eve Duncan series and I was quite sad that Johnsen decided that Joe Quinn was a better match for Eve. However, now I'm not sad anymore because in this book Logan and Sarah have to work to find a kidnapped man and stop a madman that has a grudge against Logan. And, </span>
  <span id="freeText639519575266395076" style="display:none">Iris Johansen has managed to write a story that instead of focusing on Eve Duncan (who is the main character in this series) is putting Sarah Patrick and John Logan in focus and I loved it! I adored John Logan in the first book in the Eve Duncan series and I was quite sad that Johnsen decided that Joe Quinn was a better match for Eve. However, now I'm not sad anymore because in this book Logan and Sarah have to work to find a kidnapped man and stop a madman that has a grudge against Logan. And, they work very well together and like with Eve, Logan and Sarah's "relationship" doesn't start off that good. Can have something to do with the fact that Logan forced Sarah to help Eve in the past book...<br /><br />This series is one of my favorite and, despite that Eve and Quinn have a minor role in this book is the book pretty awesome. But, as I stated above, I adore Logan so getting a book with him in the center again was a bonus. The story is intense and captivating and I loved every minute of it. Logan and Sarah have a lot of chemistry and I enjoyed their banter. And, I loved Monty, Sarah's golden retriever. It almost feels like they have telepathic communication with each other. Almost? I actually do believe so, to be honest. Another character that I came to like very much is Logan's pal Sean Galen. A fun-loving mercenary that loves to cook. <br /><br /><b>It's a wonderful book, hell it's a wonderful series! Read it!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="639519575266395076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Romance gets involved - both with Sarah and Monty. Kind of a goofy story.</span>

<div id="review_664145845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/664145845" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3764632-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309730121p2/3764632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/664145845?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/3764632-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer664145845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4859136180706443047">Gah, another one I didn't realize was a romance. Maybe I just need to stick to authors I know. It seems like all these romances stick to a formula. Take a man and woman who hate each other. Put them in a tense, stressful situation where they are forced to share physical space. They have wild sex. And more sex. One of them has commitment issues/is in denial about his or her feelings. Cue another tense/stressful situation where they are forced apart. The denial falls away and they realize they are</span>
  <span id="freeText4859136180706443047" style="display:none">Gah, another one I didn't realize was a romance. Maybe I just need to stick to authors I know. It seems like all these romances stick to a formula. Take a man and woman who hate each other. Put them in a tense, stressful situation where they are forced to share physical space. They have wild sex. And more sex. One of them has commitment issues/is in denial about his or her feelings. Cue another tense/stressful situation where they are forced apart. The denial falls away and they realize they are madly in love. They are reunited, express that love, and live happily ever after. Blah. That being said, this one didn't bother me as much as some others. It was an interesting story, especially the dog and the search and rescue operations. There also weren't any graphic sex scenes. I might pick up this author again at a used book sale, which is where I got this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4859136180706443047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189062772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17992952308389585261">I enjoyed this book however, I am not sure why it is in with the Eve Duncan series. There were maybe a dozen pages dedicated to Eve. This story focused on Sarah Patrick and Monty who we were introduced to in the previous book, The Killing Game, and her relationship with John Logan.<br/><br/>This story gave insight to Sarah and what the hold that Madden had over her and about the relationship between her and John Logan. I think the story focused more on their relationship than it did on the threat from Rud</span>
  <span id="freeText17992952308389585261" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book however, I am not sure why it is in with the Eve Duncan series. There were maybe a dozen pages dedicated to Eve. This story focused on Sarah Patrick and Monty who we were introduced to in the previous book, The Killing Game, and her relationship with John Logan.<br /><br />This story gave insight to Sarah and what the hold that Madden had over her and about the relationship between her and John Logan. I think the story focused more on their relationship than it did on the threat from Rudzik. Though, Rudzik did play a part in Login's past, it gave the reader an insite as to what he was like before and to the reason that Rudzik whated to harm Logan.<br /><br />The story takes you to Columbia in the beginning to rescue a hostage which you quickly find out is about Logan. It then returns to ranch of Sarah in Arizona where a big chuck of the story is played out. You see Logan following Sarah to Taiwin for a search/rescue of a mudslide which was created for Logan, and then they all go back to Arizona. They finally end up in North Dakota where one of Logan's plants are located, and the story finally ends there. The story does throw in a love intrest for Monty, yes Monty the dog--but not sure how believable that can be as he falls for a wolf? Seriously?<br /><br />My biggest question next to why this is in the Eve Duncan series is about Bonnie. It states in the beginning of the story that she (her bones), were found, verified via DNA, and buried on the hill by the cabin that Eve and Joe have. I have read some further books in the Eve Duncan series (can not remember which ones--maybe you can help me name them), in which Eve is still looking for Bonnie. I know I have missed some books in the series and I am now reading them in order as maybe one of the ones I have missed will explain it to me about Eve still looking for Bonnie. Maybe a goodreads person here can help me on this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17992952308389585261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10085536347683371050">~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br/><i>Blurb: He strikes without warning....he kills without mercy....he's only just begun....<br/><br/>Iris Johansen, the New York Times bestselling author of The Killing Game and The Face of Deception, delivers a gripping new novel of breathtaking suspense and explosive adventure.   <span id="freeText10085536347683371050" style="display:none">~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><i>Blurb: He strikes without warning....he kills without mercy....he's only just begun....<br /><br />Iris Johansen, the New York Times bestselling author of The Killing Game and The Face of Deception, delivers a gripping new novel of breathtaking suspense and explosive adventure. It is the story of a courageous woman who is coerced into tracking down a ruthless killer--but as she hunts out her prey with stunning accuracy, she becomes the object of his wrath....<br /><br />As part of an elite K-9 search and rescue team, Sarah Patrick and her golden retriever, Monty, have a gift for finding what no one else can--whether it's a survivor buried alive by an earthquake or the skeleton of a murdered child. But their latest assignment is not like the others. This time Sarah is being forced to take part in a deadly mission...by a man who knows enough about her past to ensure her cooperation. A man who won't take no for an answer. John Logan is used to getting what he wants, and what he wants now is Sarah's help. His top-secret venture has been sabotaged, its facilities destroyed, and its handpicked staff massacred. The sole survivor is being held for ransom. Logan knows that the only way to save the man--and the secrets he holds--is to find him as soon as possible.<br /><br />Smart, tough, and uncompromising, Sarah is furious when she is strong-armed into joining Logan on his search. And once she takes the perilous assignment, she realizes that Logan's promises that she and Monty will be safe may not be enough to protect them. Because a killer is devising a sadistic vengeance...and he may soon find use for Sarah. Racing against time to stop the bloodshed before more victims are claimed, both Sarah and Logan will look straight into the heart of true evil. And when the killer's search for revenge finally ends, no one will ever be the same again....<br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~</i></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1151953537?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/11382577-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=strong-female-characters">strong-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=action-thriller">action-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1151953537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10473603682001449229">Iris Johansen is a solid, strong author, and her books can be depended upon for interesting characters, exciting storylines, and lots of suspense and action. This was no different, and I enjoyed it.<br/><br/>The story tosses you right into the thick of the action from the very first page. Although there are ebbs and flows, the excitement is maintained pretty consistently throughout the entire book. Johansen knows how to write a story that keeps you turning pages, and this one did that for me.<br/><br/>I also loved </span>
  <span id="freeText10473603682001449229" style="display:none">Iris Johansen is a solid, strong author, and her books can be depended upon for interesting characters, exciting storylines, and lots of suspense and action. This was no different, and I enjoyed it.<br /><br />The story tosses you right into the thick of the action from the very first page. Although there are ebbs and flows, the excitement is maintained pretty consistently throughout the entire book. Johansen knows how to write a story that keeps you turning pages, and this one did that for me.<br /><br />I also loved the character of Sarah. Strong female characters always make a book a good read for me, and Sarah is definitely strong, and determined to maintain her independence no matter what, or who tries to protect her. Not only does that make for a good character, the stubbornness makes for a suspensful and engaging read.<br /><br />I will voice one minor irritant, which is not a complaint about this book, per se, as I've come across this scenario in several books I've read just recently, but just a curmudgeonly observation. How is it that these "average" women seem to constantly be thrown together with these millionares and billionaires? It seems to me that such men [and of course, they're ALWAYS men!] would have so many "people" handling their affairs, that the potential for ordinary mortals to end up face-to-face with them would be relatively small. Even smaller is the likelihood of these millionaires falling head-over-heels for such normal folks. But, as I said, that's not a complaint about this book, just something I've been noticing.<br /><br />Overall, I found this a good light read. Well-written, interesting plot, and characters I can connect to and root for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10473603682001449229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7507024894668708482" style="display:none">Oh my gosh he's doing it again. This guy sticks to a pattern. <div id="review_2507731526" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2507731526" />
    <a title="Paul Weiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss"><img alt="Paul Weiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453113069p2/51664350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2507731526?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Weiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Weiss" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss">Paul Weiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2507731526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer317542262390302252"><b>Thrilling brain candy at its finest!</b><br/><br/>John Logan, ultra-rich businessman, entrepreneur and power broker, has a serious problem. Devastated by the recent death of his Korean wife, Chen Li, from leukemia, he pulls out all the stops on the development of an artificial blood substitute at his state of the art research facility in South America. When the lab is destroyed by a saboteur's bomb and one of his key employees is kidnapped, Logan is determined to find the culprits at all costs, rescue the kid</span>
  <span id="freeText317542262390302252" style="display:none"><b>Thrilling brain candy at its finest!</b><br /><br />John Logan, ultra-rich businessman, entrepreneur and power broker, has a serious problem. Devastated by the recent death of his Korean wife, Chen Li, from leukemia, he pulls out all the stops on the development of an artificial blood substitute at his state of the art research facility in South America. When the lab is destroyed by a saboteur's bomb and one of his key employees is kidnapped, Logan is determined to find the culprits at all costs, rescue the kidnap victim and finish the project at a second laboratory in the U.S. Unscrupulously pulling on any string he can, he all but blackmails Sarah Patrick and her extraordinary dog, Monty, members of an elite K-9 ATF search and rescue unit, into helping him in a near impossible jungle rescue. When the nasty of the piece catches sight of Sarah and Monty at work, he promptly adds them to his hit list and Logan realizes his duty to protect Sarah and Monty will stretch the limits of every resource on which he can draw!<br /><br /><b>The Search</b> is brain candy at its finest and makes no pretense at aspiring to become literature! Johansen has given us a fine story - a strong female character; a strong male character; conflict between the two that allows each of their characters full rein; a romance that develops realistically without falling into the trap of being overwrought or silly; a psychopathic villain whose nastiness knows no bounds; love of animals (my wife would say that any story with "paws" is OK with her!); and, finally, a realistic glimpse into the selfless dedication of those men, women and animals that are part of disaster search and rescue teams.<br /><br />Two thumbs up for a thoroughly enjoyable thriller! I'll be looking for Johansen's next story to see where she takes the tale of Logan and Patrick's romance.<br /><br />Paul Weiss<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="317542262390302252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_481323067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481323067" />
    <a title="Kelly Stine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14904179-kelly-stine"><img alt="Kelly Stine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353876946p2/14904179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481323067?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Stine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Stine" href="/user/show/14904179-kelly-stine">Kelly Stine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553582123" href="/book/show/1294633.The_Search">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481323067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18107542799886615527">I've just recently started reading the Eve Duncan books - I picked up many of them at used book sales over the years, but then they got buried by other books. I recently uncovered them, and started reading the Search, and realized that although Eve Duncan was never mentioned in the back cover summary, it was part of the series, 3rd in the series to be exact! So I needed to back up, and start at the beginning. I've been finding them to be very suspenseful, with engaging characters.<br/><br/>THE SEARCH, act</span>
  <span id="freeText18107542799886615527" style="display:none">I've just recently started reading the Eve Duncan books - I picked up many of them at used book sales over the years, but then they got buried by other books. I recently uncovered them, and started reading the Search, and realized that although Eve Duncan was never mentioned in the back cover summary, it was part of the series, 3rd in the series to be exact! So I needed to back up, and start at the beginning. I've been finding them to be very suspenseful, with engaging characters.<br /><br />THE SEARCH, actually features billionaire John Logan for his 3rd appearance, and Search and Rescue expert, Sarah Patrick and her S&amp;R partner Monty - a very sensitive and intelligent wonder dog. Logan has an old nemesis trying to destroy all of his work, and the people around him, and thus Sarah and Monty eventually become targets. <br /><br />In the Eve Duncan books, I've been very interested in the author's careful descriptions of the forensic sculpting process. In THE SEARCH, I was very pleased with the careful and detailed descriptions of the life and passions of Search and Rescue personnel, and the close and devoted partnerships with their K9 partners.<br /><br />In each of the Iris Johansen books I've read recently, there is a twist at the end, and I have to admit, I didn't guess them before the reveal in any of them, yet. I love twists that surprise me. THE SEARCH was no different, and again, I didn't guess it. I'm not sure yet if I'm disappointed in myself, or impressed by the author's ability to fool me. I think it will take a few more books before I decide.<br /><br />If you like fast paced suspenseful stories, that features forensics, with enjoyable characters that you can empathize with, and great little twists, I think you'll enjoy this book and the others in the series, as well as the author's stand alone novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18107542799886615527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

But their latest assignment is not like the others. This time Sarah is being forced to take part in a deadly mission ... by a man who knows enough about her past to ensure her cooperation.<br/><br/>Billionaire John Logan's top-secret venture has been sabotaged, its facilities destroyed, and its handpicked staff massacred. The sole survivor is being held for ransom. </span>
  <span id="freeText12571236420481272443" style="display:none">"As part of an elite K-9 search and rescue team, Sarah Patrick and her golden retriever, Monty, have a gift for finding what no one else can. But their latest assignment is not like the others. This time Sarah is being forced to take part in a deadly mission ... by a man who knows enough about her past to ensure her cooperation.<br /><br />Billionaire John Logan's top-secret venture has been sabotaged, its facilities destroyed, and its handpicked staff massacred. The sole survivor is being held for ransom. Logan knows that the only way to save the man -- and the secrets he holds -- is to find him as soon as possible.<br />Sarah is furious when she is strong-armed into joining Logan on his search. And once she takes the perilous assignment, not even Logan's promises that she and Monty will be safe may be enough to protect them. Because a killer is devising a sadistic vengeance ... and he may soon find use for Sarah"<br /><br />This was another pretty fast paced book in the Eve Duncan series that wraps up a few things from the previous books. (No spoilers.) It's also another revolving shelf book I borrowed, so I figured I'd continue the series, because the story lines aren't too bad. I just wish Ms. Johansen would learn a better descriptor than "moistened his/her" lips--or at the very least find better places to use them. For example, Logan pulls out an automatic weapon in the jungles of South America and that's Sarah's response? (No, she wasn't turned on. It's not every day you see a billionaire business man pull out a military grade weapon.) At least there were less such instances. I have no problem with the word (I'll spare using it for the misophonics here, just the idiotic context; I get that she was a romance writer, but at least her editors are catching on.) </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9431986082270124631">This was my first Iris Johansen novel, and I loved it. My super cool therapist Grandmother gave me this book a while back and told me that it was a super good book, with tons of emotional tugs and hooks.   <span id="freeText9431986082270124631" style="display:none">This was my first Iris Johansen novel, and I loved it. My super cool therapist Grandmother gave me this book a while back and told me that it was a super good book, with tons of emotional tugs and hooks. I never realized this book was part of a whole series, with all different perspectives on characters, I did feel that this book can and does portray a great story and can be read separately from the rest of the stories. The high intensity thrill moments of this book really shows you how a real rescue dog and owner get to go encounter in their daily life's you can put yourself inside of theses characters really well, which I really liked, being a young adult trying to discover what I would like to do with my life, this book has given me just the littlest of incites of what it could be like if I became some sort of rescue agent. This book has tons of well researched subjects, I find myself watching a lot of Netflix in the late hours of the night and I mainly watch the criminal mystery shows like Criminal Minds and NCIS, and after watching those shows for hours on end and then ending my day with this book, I could see some of the topics would transfer over, the psychological factors of both or a more specific example is the small fact of how dogs smell, which I found really interesting, as I have a golden retriever myself and now wonder what goes on in her mind every time she looks at me. I really enjoyed this book and recommend others to read more books like this.</span>

<div id="review_2489383393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2489383393" />
    <a title="Mandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57057993-mandy"><img alt="Mandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538756454p2/57057993.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2489383393?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy" href="/user/show/57057993-mandy">Mandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2489383393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10620257805190183100">Okay, I admit it...I actually liked this one.<br/><br/>True, it contained all the hallmarks of an Iris Johansen novel: Strong Female Character, creepy, rapey love interest, obnoxious, one-word sentences (and a dog who communicates telepathically using only those kinds of sentences), "His lips twisted," "She stiffened," etc. We also get to see Jane be her obnoxious, bratty self.<br/><br/>There's also the fact that John Logan, from the very beginning, is one of the most infuriating love interests I've ever seen. He o</span>
  <span id="freeText10620257805190183100" style="display:none">Okay, I admit it...I actually liked this one.<br /><br />True, it contained all the hallmarks of an Iris Johansen novel: Strong Female Character, creepy, rapey love interest, obnoxious, one-word sentences (and a dog who communicates telepathically using only those kinds of sentences), "His lips twisted," "She stiffened," etc. We also get to see Jane be her obnoxious, bratty self.<br /><br />There's also the fact that John Logan, from the very beginning, is one of the most infuriating love interests I've ever seen. He outright kidnaps Sarah Douglas, using a senator who's manipulating her to force her to cooperate. I was furious about this, because I knew she'd end up sleeping with him. I was fully prepared to hate this book.<br /><br /><i>But....</i><br /><br />I didn't hate it. In fact, for the most part, I enjoyed reading it. This <i>was</i> published in 2000, and I've heard from some people that Johansen's earlier books in the Eve Duncan series are better, but I've read both "The Killing Game" (which precedes this book in the series) and "Body of Lies" (which follows it), and I didn't like either of them. Maybe it's because I hated Jane in the former, and Joe in the latter, and both characters were mostly absent in this one. <br /><br />But, no, that's not fair. I actually thought this was a good story, which you will almost never hear me say about one of Johansen's books. She had an interesting idea for a villain, and the mystery of John's late wife, Chen Li, kept me curious and wanting to see what her story was. I am curious, though. John said that he met Chen Li in Japan. Does Johansen think "Chen Li" is a Japanese name? It's not. I mean, I don't <i>think</i> Iris Jo is that dense, but I know there are plenty of people who pull that "all Asian languages sound the same" crap.<br /><br />So, what else was different about this book?<br /><br />Johansen is actually fairly good at suspense, but this time I actually <i>felt</i> it. I could feel the sense of urgency every time Sarah began to search for someone or something. I was also pulled in to the emotions of the characters in the story, which is something new for her books. The whole scene at the village of Kai Chi was actually very touching, and felt far more real to me than most of Johansen's other attempts at emotional scenes.<br /><br />That said, I did find the descriptions of Monty's emotions to be annoying. Johansen has this habit of describing psychic connections with sentence fragments, and it's super obnoxious. It's especially bad with Monty, because he only uses a single word each time, and he tends to repeat it, like this:<br /><br /><i>Sad</i>.<br /><br />Sarah reacts to what he said.<br /><br /><i>Sad</i>.<br /><br />Sarah says something to him.<br /><br /><i>Sad</i>.<br /><br />Sarah says something else to him.<br /><br /><i>Sad</i>.<br /><br />SHUT UP ALREADY! WE GET THE POINT! HE'S SAD!<br /><br />Another weird thing about Monty is that, halfway through the book, he falls in love with a wolf. John jokes that maybe this is going to be a one-night stand, and Sarah's like, "Monty's not like that." What do you mean, he's not <i>like</i> that? Dogs don't have any concept of romance, Johansen. Or one of one-night stands, for that matter. They have an instinct to mate. I'm not saying dogs can love, but love and mating are two separate things. Monty's not going to express his love for the wolf through mating. In fact, dogs don't even mate for pleasure, and the reproductive process, to put it delicately, is not necessarily the most enjoyable of interactions. Oh, and also, Sarah didn't have Monty fixed. Why? Because Monty's "special." Ugh.<br /><br />Actually, the whole thing with the wolf was pretty pointless. Why did there need to be a beta couple in the form of a wolf and a dog? I didn't feel like it really added anything to the story. Plus, I don't know, I'm sure an employee of the Fish and Wildlife service would say Sarah broke about 50 laws by taking the wolf into her home and then just deciding to keep her. But hey, it's not like the main character doing illegal stuff and getting away with it because she has "connections" isn't a staple of Iris Jo's books.<br /><br />I must say, the entire truth behind the bad guy's involvement with Chen Li was a bit underwhelming, but I still found "The Search" to be quite a page turner, and the action continued right up to the final pages. That's about the best I can say for any thriller.<br /><br />The fact that I liked this book frustrated me. Not because I'm too proud to admit I liked a book written by Iris Johansen, but because I'm now aware of how good a book written by her can be. Previously, I've said that "Close Your Eyes" is probably the best of her books, but I actually think this one was even better. So what's the deal, Johansen?<br /><br />Personally, I feel this is the problem with a lot of super prolific writers. You know, the ones who seem to come out with a new book every year, or even more frequently. They write a few really good books, but once they become famous enough, they realize there are fans who will read whatever they write and think it's good. I mean, I have to admit, I'm not entirely innocent of this--I'm a "ride of die" fan for a couple of video game series, and have admitted the very fact that something is a new addition to one of those series is reason enough for me to like it. But that doesn't mean I can't still criticize the creator.<br /><br />Johansen and other prolific authors are certainly capable of writing a good story; however, after a while, they become far too formulaic. They settle down, comfortable in their pattern of similar stories, and stop challenging themselves. I felt similarly after reading too many of Stephen King's books.<br /><br />As a fanfic author (no, I'm not linking you), I admit I've fallen into a similar trap on occasion. Quantity over quality. Patterns I can't quite seem to shake, like the characters I'm looking to pair up having a pointless, boring discussion over food and drink. Using the same phrase waaaay too frequently. (Stop saying "basically"! Stop it!) So my beef with Johansen isn't personal.<br /><br />But I'm not expecting the rest of her books (I still have like 13 left) to be as good as this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10620257805190183100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2963898450" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2963898450" />
    <a title="Alice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4435091-alice"><img alt="Alice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480024176p2/4435091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2963898450?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2963898450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5418741414834909793">For the entire plot to balance on the hope of Eve finding her daughter, I'm surprised how this book just shoved it aside. One scene, a tiny little mention, and it's done. I followed Eve for two books because I desperately wanted her to find Bonnie, and how she would handle it, and it's just done in the peripheral. <br/><br/>But Sarah was a nice change of pace. I was scared for Monty. This was the early 2000s; anything could happen to dogs in media. Sarah's independence and love for her job, even though it</span>
  <span id="freeText5418741414834909793" style="display:none">For the entire plot to balance on the hope of Eve finding her daughter, I'm surprised how this book just shoved it aside. One scene, a tiny little mention, and it's done. I followed Eve for two books because I desperately wanted her to find Bonnie, and how she would handle it, and it's just done in the peripheral. <br /><br />But Sarah was a nice change of pace. I was scared for Monty. This was the early 2000s; anything could happen to dogs in media. Sarah's independence and love for her job, even though it's a hard job, was nice. <br /><br />Logan was the typical "I'm trying to be a nice guy" douche, but I liked learning more about him. Oh, and the romance was meh. Expected from the beginning but I didn't think it would be that bland.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5418741414834909793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ly4oLJBOEyLITZIWU+GDHZVAMzAmBlVIKqM7RJ3Qh4lQjAbSquTzlaTTqLONLLvx6SpWgcJ5hkG8R/G+aNbDWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3TUoJDUHecQgr/AAPzNAd2ygWgN1ZqDZ+eMIhulBVP8alwbaD62Zc0wxyqXh/nibEMo/spEZc9BvB8J8HEcQLQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2793827338834305063">Iris Johansen is a <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author. She began her writing after her children left home for college. She first achieved success in the early 1980s writing category romances. In 1991, Johansen began writing suspense historical romance novels, starting with the publication of <i>The Wind Dancer</i>. In 1996 Johansen switched genres, turning to crime fiction, with which she has had great su</span>
  <span id="freeText2793827338834305063" style="display:none">Iris Johansen is a <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author. She began her writing after her children left home for college. She first achieved success in the early 1980s writing category romances. In 1991, Johansen began writing suspense historical romance novels, starting with the publication of <i>The Wind Dancer</i>. In 1996 Johansen switched genres, turning to crime fiction, with which she has had great success. <br /><br />She lives in Georgia and is married. Her son, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/205479.Roy_Johansen" title="Roy Johansen" rel="nofollow noopener">Roy Johansen</a>, is an Edgar Award-winning screenwriter and novelist. Her daughter, Tamara, serves as her research assistant.<br /><br />IRIS JOHANSEN is The <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>Night and Day, Hide Away, Shadow Play, Your Next Breath, The Perfect Witness, Live to See Tomorrow, Silencing Eve, Hunting Eve, Taking Eve, Sleep No More, What Doesn't Kill You, Bonnie, Quinn, Eve, Chasing The Night, Eight Days to Live, Blood Game, Deadlock, Dark Summer, Pandora's Daughter, Quicksand, Killer Dreams, On The Run</i>, and more. And with her son, Roy Johansen, she has coauthored <i>Night Watch, The Naked Eye, Sight Unseen, Close Your Eyes, Shadow Zone, Storm Cycle,</i> and <i>Silent Thunder</i>.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.irisjohansen.com">http://www.irisjohansen.com</a></span>

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
